<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr1652164">
<a name="tr1652164"></a>
<div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0005157">Jake Lloyd</a> has said that he retired from acting because of the trauma he experienced after playing Anakin Skywalker. According to Lloyd, other children constantly teased him about the role. For example they would make lightsaber sounds whenever he walked by. Lloyd also said that the situation was made worse because, in his opinion, the film did not meet the fans' expectations. Despite this, Lloyd has reprised the role of Anakin in several video games and has appeared at Star Wars conventions/events.  </div>

<div class="sodatext">


According to Star Wars canon, Obi-Wan's hanging braid is a Jedi tradition common to all Padawan Learners. When his master feels that he has reached proper maturity, he cuts the braid with his lightsaber, signifying that the student is now a full Jedi Knight.  </div>

The sound effect when Obi-Wan Kenobi's lightsaber is kicked down the reactor shaft towards the end of the movie, is the same sound effect heard when Luke Skywalker throws his lightsaber away in <a href="/title/tt0086190">Star Wars: Episode VI - Return of the Jedi</a> (1983) when he tells the Emperor that he is a Jedi.  </div>

<div class="sodatext">


The sound of the underwater monsters growling near the beginning of the film was made by the main sound technician's three-year-old daughter. The sound of her crying was recorded, and the frequency lowered to obtain the sound heard in the film.  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr0795554">
<a name="tr0795554"></a>
<div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0000553">Liam Neeson</a> convinced <a href="/name/nm0000184">George Lucas</a> to keep a scene where Qui-Gon Jinn puts his hand on Shmi Skywalker's shoulder. Lucas felt this might be out of character for the monk-like Jedi, but Neeson thought there should be an emotional connection between the characters. In an interview with Premiere magazine, Neeson defended his action, saying, "It may be 'Star Wars', but we've got to have something in there for the adults."  </div>

<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr0795073">
<a name="tr0795073"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


At the time of the film's release, the producers ran a disinformation campaign to suggest that <a href="/name/nm0000204">Natalie Portman</a> played both Padme and The Queen at all times. In fact, they are not always the same person. For many sections of the film, notably those where The Queen is wearing the black outfit with the huge feather headdress, she is actually a decoy, played by <a href="/name/nm0461136">Keira Knightley</a>. The real queen, Portman, is actually disguised as a handmaiden. Various conflicting public statements make it extremely difficult to figure out who is who. Whole websites are devoted to figuring out which actress is playing which handmaiden or The Queen at any given point.  </div>

<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr0795538">
<a name="tr0795538"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


Scenes of straightforward dialog maybe comprised of up to 6 layers of computer-composited imagery as the following example shows. In one scene, <a href="/name/nm0000204">Natalie Portman</a>'s best take had been take seven while <a href="/name/nm0005157">Jake Lloyd</a>'s was take one. The two takes were spliced together. However, Lloyd's mouth at the end of the scene is still gaped open, so the same segment from take fifteen (in which his mouth is closed) is patched in. Furthermore, when Portman appears to look down from Lloyd instead of up, those few seconds were run backwards, which unexpectedly caused steam in the background to rise in reverse. The problem was fixed by flipping the steam backwards. All these fixes resulted in a seamless scene. This technique prompted <a href="/name/nm0000553">Liam Neeson</a>, upon the film's release, to complain thus, "We are basically puppets. I don't think I can live with the inauthenticity of movies anymore."  </div>

Dates in Star Wars are based around the Battle of Yavin (in <a href="/title/tt0076759">Star Wars</a> (1977)): <ul><li><a href="/title/tt0120915">Star Wars: Episode I - The Phantom Menace</a> (1999) takes place 32 years BBY (Before the Battle of Yavin),</li><br/><br/><li><a href="/title/tt0121765">Star Wars: Episode II - Attack of the Clones</a> (2002) is 22 BBY,</li><br/><br/><li><a href="/title/tt0121766">Star Wars: Episode III - Revenge of the Sith</a> (2005) is 19 BBY,</li><br/><br/><li><a href="/title/tt0076759">Star Wars</a> (1977): is 0 BBY,</li><br/><br/><li><a href="/title/tt0080684">Star Wars: Episode V - The Empire Strikes Back</a> (1980) is 3 years ABY (After the Battle of Yavin),</li><br/><br/><li><a href="/title/tt0086190">Star Wars: Episode VI - Return of the Jedi</a> (1983) is 4 ABY.</li><br/><br/></ul> </div>

<div class="sodatext">


In 1997, a fierce sandstorm destroyed several of the Tatooine sets in the desert outside Tozeur, Tunisia. Filming resumed two days later. <a href="/name/nm0000184">George Lucas</a> considered this a good omen, as the very same thing had happened during filming of the original <a href="/title/tt0076759">Star Wars</a> (1977).  </div>

<a name="tr0794969"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


Palpatine's line "There is no civility, there is only politics" is a corruption of part of the Jedi Code which consists of a negative assertion followed by a positive one. For example: "There is no fear, there is only calm. There is no death, there is only the Force."  </div>

<div class="sodatext">


The sound of the hovering battle tanks used by the battle droids was created by running an electric razor around a metal salad bowl and then digitally lowering the pitch.  </div>

<a name="tr0795465"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


In the original trilogy, lightsaber activations and deactivations happened off-screen most of the time to prevent the "jumps" that would occur when the film was stopped to allow the "activated" lightsaber props to be substituted for the deactivated handles. This no longer poses a problem and every activation/deactivation occurs on-screen in <a href="/title/tt0120915">Star Wars: Episode I - The Phantom Menace</a> (1999).  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr2015576">
<a name="tr2015576"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


A few USC students took the Japanese Laserdisc &amp; made their own edit of the movie. Contrary to popular belief, it does NOT cut out all scenes featuring Jar-Jar Binks, but does remove many of his sillier and more distracting moments, and makes many other minor tweaks. It became known as the "Phantom Edit". <a href="/name/nm0000184">George Lucas</a> requested to see a copy, and then Lucasfilm issued a press release reiterating that it is illegal to copy and/or edit a Lucasfilm property.  </div>

<div class="sodatext">


In both of his identities, Darth Sidious/Palpatine makes his first appearance as a hologram. This is in keeping with the original trilogy, when his first appearance was a holographic communication with Darth Vader in <a href="/title/tt0080684">Star Wars: Episode V - The Empire Strikes Back</a> (1980).  </div>

<a name="tr1717623"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


One of the first casting rumors for the alleged "Star Wars prequel", came from a science-fiction magazine called Starblazer. In their Summer 1985 issue, they published that <a href="/name/nm0000356">Sybil Danning</a> was to possibly portray the "sexy witch" that seduces Anakin Skywalker to the Dark Side. In 2012, Sybil confirmed on her Facebook page that the rumor was indeed true, and that many discussions took place at that time.  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr0795303">
<a name="tr0795303"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


Earlier drafts of the script placed more emphasis on the character of Obi-Wan Kenobi. Originally he was already a fully trained Jedi by the start of the movie and also the only Jedi negotiator sent to Naboo at the start of the movie. In this same draft, the character of Qui-Gon Jinn was not introduced until the characters reached Coruscant, and that character was of the same age of Obi-Wan, not his mentor.  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr1339450">
<a name="tr1339450"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


The announcer at the Pod Race welcomes people, "...from all the Outer Rim Territories." This is a reference to the galaxy's grouping. The Star Wars galaxy is organized in concentric circles. Starting at the center and moving outward the circles are, The Deep Core, Core, Colonies, Inner Rim, Expansion Region, Mid Rim, Outer Rim, Wild Space, Unknown Regions.  </div>

<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr0795350">
<a name="tr0795350"></a>
<div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0000184">George Lucas</a> made a similar deal as he did in the original <a href="/title/tt0076759">Star Wars</a> (1977). Both Lucas and Fox Studios agreed that he would forego his salary as a director provided he owns the entire negative of the final cut of the film as well as ancillary rights of all toys and commercial tie-ins.  </div>

<a name="tr0795464"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


Tests were conducted to see if Yoda could be realized digitally but it was determined that the technology was not up to scratch. A CG model of Yoda was nevertheless created, but only used in one shot, a long shot incidentally, during the scene on Naboo near the end where Obi-Wan Kenobi and Yoda discuss Anakin's future.  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr0795146">
<a name="tr0795146"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


When Palpatine lands at Naboo at the end of the film, he's accompanied by Senate Guards dressed in blue. The guards' costumes are similar to those of the red Emperor's guards seen in <a href="/title/tt0121765">Star Wars: Episode II - Attack of the Clones</a> (2002), <a href="/title/tt0121766">Star Wars: Episode III - Revenge of the Sith</a> (2005), and <a href="/title/tt0086190">Star Wars: Episode VI - Return of the Jedi</a> (1983), and are, in a way, predecessors to the later red guards.  </div>

<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr0795512">
<a name="tr0795512"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


Qui-Gon Jinn identifies the Queen's starship as a Nubian model J-327. "327" was the number of the landing bay where the Millennium Falcon landed on the first Death Star in <a href="/title/tt0076759">Star Wars</a> (1977) as well as the number of the landing platform in Cloud City in <a href="/title/tt0080684">Star Wars: Episode V - The Empire Strikes Back</a> (1980). During the introduction of the pod racers, one of the pods is "327".  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr0795622">
<a name="tr0795622"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


The words chanted during the "Duel of the Fates" are from <a href="/name/nm0336345">Robert Graves</a>' poem "The White Goddess". "The White Goddess" is a translation of the original version, "Cad Goddeu" or "The Battle of Achren", an early Celtic work of great antiquity also known as "The Battle of the Trees," which was originally composed by Gwion and is found in the "Book of Taliesin", a Thirteenth Century Welsh manuscript . <a href="/name/nm0002354">John Williams</a> had the lines "Under the tongue root a fight most dread, and another raging, behind, in the head" translated into Sanskrit. The translation sung in the movie is as follows: "Korah Matah Korah Rahtahmah Korah Rahtamah Yoodhah Korah Korah Syahdho Rahtahmah Daanyah Korah Keelah Daanyah Nyohah Keelah Korah Rahtahmah Syadho Keelah Korah Rahtahmah Korah Daanyah Korah Rahtahmah Korah Daanyah Korah Rahtahmah Nyohah Keelah Korah Rahtahmah Syadho Keelah Korah Rahtahmah Korah Korah Matah Korah Rahtahmah Korah Daanyah Korah Rahtahmah Nyohah Keelah Korah Rahtahmah Syadho Keelah Korah Rahtahmah Korah"  </div>

<a name="tr0795611"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


The Neimodians were originally to be computer generated creatures, but to save costs were changed into men wearing masks. Animatronic model designer <a href="/name/nm0178846">John Coppinger</a> quickly recycled animatronic masks from <a href="/title/tt0119116">The Fifth Element</a> (1997) to use as the basis for their facial movement.  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr0795630">
<a name="tr0795630"></a>
<div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0000184">George Lucas</a>'s very first draft of <a href="/title/tt0076759">Star Wars</a> (1977) began, "This is the story of Mace Windu, a revered Jedi-bendu of Opuchi who was related to Usby C.J. Thape, a padawan learner of the famed Jedi." Both the character of Mace Windu and the concept of padawan learners make their first appearance in <a href="/title/tt0120915">Star Wars: Episode I - The Phantom Menace</a> (1999).  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr0795488">
<a name="tr0795488"></a>
<div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0000184">George Lucas</a> asked <a href="/name/nm0001410">Lawrence Kasdan</a> to write the script (and possibly for <a href="/title/tt0121765">Star Wars: Episode II - Attack of the Clones</a> (2002) and <a href="/title/tt0121766">Star Wars: Episode III - Revenge of the Sith</a> (2005) as well), but he turned it down because he thought with <a href="/title/tt0080684">Star Wars: Episode V - The Empire Strikes Back</a> (1980) and <a href="/title/tt0086190">Star Wars: Episode VI - Return of the Jedi</a> (1983), Lucas's relationship to the movies had taken one step back and that he alone should take responsibility and make exactly the movie he wanted to make.  </div>

<div class="sodatext">


C3P0 was originally only supposed to appear in scenes set in and around the slave quarters. During post production <a href="/name/nm0000184">George Lucas</a> decided to optically add the droid to several outside scenes.  </div>

The Jedi Council set was too large to be saved, only the chairs were put in storage. For <a href="/title/tt0121765">Star Wars: Episode II - Attack of the Clones</a> (2002) and <a href="/title/tt0121766">Star Wars: Episode III - Revenge of the Sith</a> (2005), backgrounds plates from <a href="/title/tt0120915">Star Wars: Episode I - The Phantom Menace</a> (1999) were reused.  </div>

<a name="tr0795258"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


The name used by the Queen while in disguise (and, later, after her term as Queen ends), "Padme", is the Sanskrit word for "lotus". "Yoda" is also derived from the Sanskrit word for "warrior".  </div>

<a name="tr0795373"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


"Phantom Menace" was the name of a villain in the "Flash Gordon" comics. The same name used by NASA to refer to the fact that so few of their attempts to send a probe to Mars were successful, to the point that the missions seemed cursed.  </div>

<a name="tr1598311"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


Almost 12 years after the film was released, <a href="/name/nm0000553">Liam Neeson</a> (Qui-Gon Jinn) and <a href="/name/nm0000278">Pernilla August</a> (Shmi Skywalker) both reprised their roles in _"Star Wars: The Clone Wars" (2008) {Overlords (#3.15)}" (2011)_. Neeson would later do so again in _"Star Wars: The Clone Wars" (2008) {Ghosts of Mortis (#3.17)}" (2011).  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr0795081">
<a name="tr0795081"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


In the summer of 1998, the movie <a href="/title/tt0120685">Godzilla</a> (1998) was released amongst a whirlwind of media hype as part an ambitious studio campaign called "Size Does Matter", featuring massive signs and banners meant to emphasize the size of the monster. After its release, the movie was the subject of an intense backlash by both critics and audiences. The programmers of www.StarWars.com put up a temporary webpage with mocking the "Godzilla" campaign with a poster lettered with the green glow reading "Plot Does Matter - May 1999", in reference to <a href="/title/tt0120915">Star Wars: Episode I - The Phantom Menace</a> (1999).  </div>

<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr1924614">
<a name="tr1924614"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


The planet "Tatooine" was named after the town Tataouine in Tunisia. Close to that town took place the shooting of the scenes of "Mos Espa" in July 1997.  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr0795033">
<a name="tr0795033"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


Theatres receiving the first trailer and posters were warned in writing to return them to the distributor (Twentieth Century Fox) on time or risk not receiving further media, and possibly the film itself. This was done to attempt to prevent the "black-market" sale of the incredibly popular trailer.  </div>

<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr0795181">
<a name="tr0795181"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


The design of Queen Amidala's starship, in which she escapes Naboo with Qui-Gonn and Obi-Wan, was inspired by the Lockheed Martin SR-71 "Blackbird" reconnaissance jet.  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr0795499">
<a name="tr0795499"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


In earlier drafts, the name of the planet where Queen Amidala comes from was called Utapau. This name was also used and abandoned in the early-1970s drafts of <a href="/title/tt0076759">Star Wars</a> (1977), and was finally used for the sinkhole planet where Obi-Wan confronts General Grievous in <a href="/title/tt0121766">Star Wars: Episode III - Revenge of the Sith</a> (2005).  </div>

<a name="tr0794973"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


The Battle Droids were originally supposed to be as white as the Stormtroopers from the original trilogy. During pre production <a href="/name/nm0000184">George Lucas</a> decided to change them to beige.  </div>

<div class="sodatext">


Anakin has two model ships on his bed in Tatooine. These are models of early designs considered for the Naboo Starfighters. In the documentaries on the DVD, we see these models being rejected by <a href="/name/nm0000184">George Lucas</a>.  </div>

<a name="tr0795196"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


Before 'Samuel L Jackson' expressed his interest in joining the cast, Mace Windu was to be an animatronic character. This alien, was later identified as an 'Anx' and can be seen sitting in Watto's box during the pod race (as Graxol Kelvyyn) as well as during the senate scenes (as Senator Horox Ryyder).  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr0795085">
<a name="tr0795085"></a>
<div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0001160">Adrian Dunbar</a> was originally cast as Bail Organa and made a brief appearance in the senate sequence. When his performance was cut, the character's name was changed to Bail Antilles (mentioned on screen by Captain Panaka). A picture of Dunbar still appeared in two publications: The Ultimate Star Wars Episode I Sticker Book (as Senator Bail Organa) and Star Wars Episode I Who's Who (as Bail Antilles).  </div>

Qui-Gon Jinn's name is not given in dialogue until 38 minutes into the film when he introduces himself to Shmi Skywalker (<a href="/name/nm0000278">Pernilla August</a>), whose first name is not actually mentioned until <a href="/title/tt0121765">Star Wars: Episode II - Attack of the Clones</a> (2002).  </div>

<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr1998283">
<a name="tr1998283"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


The interiors of the palace on Naboo were shot in an Italian palace, the Reggia Reale (Royal Palace) of Caserta (now used mostly as a museum). However, the palace had candelabras on the wall which had to be removed prior to shooting. One of the curators, there to watch that the crew doesn't make damages, played one of Amidala's counselors.  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr2028299">
<a name="tr2028299"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


Early treatments of the film originally did not have Qui-Gon Jinn, and simply had Obi-Wan by himself as a Jedi Knight. Qui-Gon was added as Obi-Wan's master to flow with the generational "Passing the Torch" theme found throughout the whole saga.  </div>

<div class="sodatext">


In the German language version of the film, the collaborating Trade Federation leaders have a French accent, while in the Italian language version they have heavy Russian accents. They also have Russian accents in the Czech version, except for the Viceroy, who speaks fluent Czech for reasons unknown.  </div>

<div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0000184">George Lucas</a> approached <a href="/name/nm0002376">David Hare</a> to write the screenplay and even co-direct the film. Lucas confessed he had reservations about working with the actors, and hoped that he could focus on the action while Hare focused on the acting. Hare declined.  </div>

The name "Qui Gon" derives from an ancient Chinese system of alternative medicine called "Qigong". The "Jinn" part refers to the "Djinn" or genies of Arabian myth.  </div>

<div class="sodatext">


The Naboo Palace setting was also the ballroom set for the Frankenstein family mansion in Geneva used in <a href="/title/tt0109836">Frankenstein</a> (1994). <a href="/name/nm0408309">Celia Imrie</a> appears in both movies.  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr1621666">
<a name="tr1621666"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


The planet Naboo is heavily influenced by Italian Renaissance design and architecture, and the stadium where the pod race takes place is based upon Roman designs of the early Christian era.  </div>

<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr0795401">
<a name="tr0795401"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


To fill all the Senate Pods, teams of extras (mostly Lucasfilm employees) were filmed separately. Some of them were shot on digital video. Enough library footage of Senators was gathered to populate the Senate scenes of both <a href="/title/tt0121765">Star Wars: Episode II - Attack of the Clones</a> (2002) and <a href="/title/tt0121766">Star Wars: Episode III - Revenge of the Sith</a> (2005).  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr0795682">
<a name="tr0795682"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


While <a href="/name/nm0000553">Liam Neeson</a> did the majority of his own stunts, he did have three stunt doubles on hand to do everything else. <a href="/name/nm1741713">Andrew Lawden</a> doubled for Neeson for part of the Darth Maul duel on Tatooine, while <a href="/name/nm0332980">Joss Gower</a> played Qui-Gon for some shots in the main duel near the end. <a href="/name/nm0408449">Rob Inch</a> did everything else.  </div>

<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr1998282">
<a name="tr1998282"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


The crew was considering giving the Neimoidians an alien language with subtitles translating this into English (similar to other alien species in the franchise), but decided not to since the Neimoidians carried the "political element" of the film and did not want to detract from this.  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr1998286">
<a name="tr1998286"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


The "buzzing" sound of Captain Panaka's portable radio is actually a "ray pistol" from the 1950s. The same sound effect was used in the original Star Wars for the restraining bolts on droids.  </div>

<div class="sodatext">


It appears that the other head of the podrace announcer is simply saying the same thing as the first head, but in Huttesse instead of English. This isn't so. Originally what the second head said was supposed to be subtitled, and the screenplay of the movie contains a translation of all of his dialogue.  </div>

Although Nute Gunray (<a href="/name/nm0141324">Silas Carson</a>) and Shmi Skywalker (<a href="/name/nm0000278">Pernilla August</a>) are both major supporting characters in the film, neither character's name is stated in dialogue until <a href="/title/tt0121765">Star Wars: Episode II - Attack of the Clones</a> (2002).  </div>

<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr0795431">
<a name="tr0795431"></a>
<div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0781181">Andy Secombe</a> based his vocal performance of Watto on <a href="/name/nm0000027">Alec Guinness</a>' performance as Fagin in <a href="/title/tt0040662">Oliver Twist</a> (1948). So essentially, Anakin is passed from one Alec Guinness impersonator to another through the course of the film.  </div>

The Republic Cruiser seen at the beginning of the film is based on an early concept design for the Rebel Blockade Runner from <a href="/title/tt0076759">Star Wars</a> (1977).  </div>

<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr0795537">
<a name="tr0795537"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


Two conflicting stories have come out of LucasFilm on the origin of the Nemoidians' name. One version says that the the aquatically-evolved aliens were named as an allusion to the fictional naval character, Capt. Nemo. According to other sources, however, the race was named for sci-fi icon <a href="/name/nm0000559">Leonard Nimoy</a>.  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr2291851">
<a name="tr2291851"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


On his way to England to be fitted for the suit of Jar Jar Binks, <a href="/name/nm0078886">Ahmed Best</a> suffered severe burns when hot tea was spilled into his lap. Best endured great pain while a cast of his body was made but told no one about his injury, unwilling to take any chance that might jeopardize his role.  </div>

<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr2073798">
<a name="tr2073798"></a>
<div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm1020089">Sally Hawkins</a> was an extra, while attending drama school. She was on set for one day, as a friend was able to give her access. She was paid 100 quid for playing an extra in the village and wore a chiffon costume. On set she saw <a href="/name/nm0000191">Ewan McGregor</a> while he was playing football, but din't talk to him. Years later she co-starred with him in <a href="/title/tt0795493">Cassandra's Dream</a> (2007) but has never told him they had previously "co-starred".  </div>

<div class="sodatext">


Several crew members and actors had recurring or multiple supporting roles in the film. Among them Jerome Blake played a number of alien characters, Mike Savva was a captured Naboo ground crew tech and also a Naboo Guard, later appearing as the Naboo Guard at the beginning of Attack Of The Clones.  </div>

<div class="sodatext">


According to <a href="/name/nm0078886">Ahmed Best</a> in a Rolling Stone article, <a href="/name/nm0001391">Michael Jackson</a> "campaigned" for the role of Jar Jar Binks, but <a href="/name/nm0000184">George Lucas</a> decided against casting him because his star status would "compromise" the film. At one point, Lucas took Best and <a href="/name/nm0000204">Natalie Portman</a> backstage at a concert and introduced Best to Jackson to gain the singer's approval.  </div>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr2362931">
<a name="tr2362931"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


According to revised Star Wars canon, Darth Maul did not die when Obi-Wan sliced him in two. While falling down the pit, Maul grabbed at a maintenance hatch and swung into a disposal tube. The impact of landing knocked him out. Later, garbage collection droids dumped him into a trash bin which was shipped to an offworld refuse dump. Maul existed there for twelve years, a broken half-mad cripple, until he was eventually rescued by his brother, Savage Oppress.  </div>

<h4 class="li_group">SpoilersÂ </h4>

<div class="soda odd sodavote" id="tr0795122">
<a name="tr0795122"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


Darth Maul only blinks once throughout the film. This is mostly because the contact lenses that <a href="/name/nm0661917">Ray Park</a> wore made it difficult to blink and Park liked the idea of a villain who never stops staring. He blinks when he is stabbed by Obi-Wan Kenobi  </div>

<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr1998304">
<a name="tr1998304"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


According to the Blu-ray commentary, <a href="/name/nm0000184">George Lucas</a> was sensitive to the amount of violence he was putting into the movie. He was strongly debating over whether or not to include Darth Maul's death of being sliced in half, which he decided was necessary to leave no doubt in viewers' minds that Maul was dead.  </div>

<div class="sodatext">


This is the only film in the series in which the top-credited actor (<a href="/name/nm0000553">Liam Neeson</a> as Qui-Gon Jinn) plays a non-recurring character, and in which the top-credited character dies.     Â <span class="ghost">|</span>Â 
    <a href="/title/tt0120915/trivia?item=tr1998303">Permalink</a>
<a class="hidesoda hidden" href="#">HideÂ options</a>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="soda even sodavote" id="tr2159186">
<a name="tr2159186"></a>
<div class="sodatext">


During the battle between Qui-Gon Jin and Obi-Wan Kenobi against Darth Maul, A total of 9 strikes are landed without the use of the lightsaber blade.  Darth Maul lands a kick on each Jedi in the main hanger, Darth Maul lands a kick against Obi-Wan causing him to fall to a lower platform, Qui-Gon lands an elbow and punch combination to knock Darth Maul to a lower platform, Darth Maul uses a kick as a counterattack after Qui-Gon jumps from a lower platform, Darth Maul uses the hilt of his lightsaber before fatally stabbing Qui-Gon, Obi-Wan lands a kick on Darth Maul after breaking his lightsaber in half, Darth Maul lands a kick on Obi-Wan causing him to completely flip over and land on his feet, and Darth Maul uses a force push to knock Obi-Wan into the chasm.  </div>
<div class="did-you-know-actions">
<a class="interesting-count-text" href="?item=tr2159186"> 12 of 15 found this interesting</a>
